                .addSize([0, 0], [640, 480])
                .build()

        gptSubPage = window.digitalData && digitalData.page && digitalData.page.subPage ? digitalData.page.subPage : "blank";

        function gptClean(gptText) {
            if (typeof (gptText) == "string") {
                gptText = gptText.replace(/\&/g, '%26');
                return gptText.replace(/\^|\*|#|\$|\"|\'|\=|\,|\!|\+|\~|\;|\(|\)|\<|\>|\[|\]|\?|\%|\:|\@|\;|\&|\||\{|\}|\\|/g, '');
            }
            return "blank";
        }

        googletag.pubads()
            .setTargeting('property', 'value-of-property')    // Change and duplicate this line for as many additional keywords to send
            .setTargeting('doi', gptClean('10.1002/adfm.202406915')) // Publication DOI
            .setTargeting('pbPage', gptClean(gptPage))
            .setTargeting('pbSubPage', gptClean(gptSubPage))
            .setTargeting('urlpath', gptClean(document.location.pathname));

        googletag.defineSlot($GooglePublisherCategory, 'fluid', 'advert-leaderboard')
            .defineSizeMapping(sizes.leaderboard)
            .addService(googletag.pubads())
            .setCollapseEmptyDiv(true);

    <script type="text/javascript" nonce="dad687aaa99442848dad211506cec98c">

        function getParameter(parameterName) {
            let result = null,
                tmp = [];
            location.search
                .substr(1)
                .split("&")
                .forEach(function (item) {
                    tmp = item.split("=");
                    if (tmp[0] === parameterName) result = tmp[1];
                });
            return result;
        }

        var SeamlessAccessService = {
            spUrl: "/action/ssostart",
            returnURL: window.location.href,
            my_context: 'seamlessaccess.org',
            queryParamsDelimiter: encodeURIComponent('?'),

            getWAYFLessUrl: function (entityId) {
                let redirectURL = getParameter('redirectUri');
                if(redirectURL == null){
                    redirectURL = encodeURIComponent(this.returnURL);
                }
                if(redirectURL.indexOf('saml_referrer') < 0){
                    redirectURL += encodeURIComponent(((redirectURL.indexOf(this.queryParamsDelimiter) !== -1) ? '&' : '?') + 'saml_referrer');
                }
                return this.spUrl + "?idp=" + encodeURIComponent(entityId)
                    + "&redirectUri=" + redirectURL;
            },
            retrieveEntity: function () {
                var self = this;
                var ps = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    ps.entities(self.my_context)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // get the results
                            var results = res.data;
                            return resolve(results);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            reject('retrieve entity error: ' + err);
                        });
                });
            },
            updateEntity: function (entitydata) {
                var self = this;
                var ps = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                var jsonObj = {};
                try {
                    //try to parse it, if it is a json string
                    jsonObj = JSON.parse(entitydata.val());
                } catch (e) {
                    jsonObj = entitydata;
                }
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    ps.update(self.my_context, jsonObj)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // Process the results
                            var ssoInstitutions = res.data;
                            return resolve(ssoInstitutions);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to update the local storage duo to: ' + err);
                            reject(err);
                        });
                })
            },
            removeEntity: function (entityId) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    persistService.remove(self.my_context, entityId)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to remove from local storage duo to: ' + err);
                        });
                })
            },
            getAccessibleEntityStatus: function (doi, entityId, entityTitle) {
                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    $.ajax({
                        type: 'POST',
                        url: '/action/seamlessAccess',
                        accept: {
                            text: "application/json"
                        },
                        data: {doi: doi, entityid: entityId, entityTitle: entityTitle, eventGroupKey: '0aa63e9e-38ce-4f6b-8752-81d6d9ecf0b0'}

                    }).done(function (status) {
                        return resolve(status);
                    });
                });
            },
            getEntitiesWithAllInfo: function (doi) {
                let self = this,
                    arrayOfPromises = [];
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    self.retrieveEntity().then(function (res) {
                        let allSsoInstitutions = res;
                        for (let i in allSsoInstitutions) {
                            let ssoInstitution = allSsoInstitutions[i];
                            arrayOfPromises.push(new Promise(function (resolve) {
                                self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, ssoInstitution.entity.entityID, ssoInstitution.entity.title)
                                    .then(function (entityStatus) {
                                        resolve({
                                            entityID: ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,
                                            entityTitle: ssoInstitution.entity.title,
                                            entityStatusObj: entityStatus,
                                            entitySsoUrl: self.getWAYFLessUrl(ssoInstitution.entity.entityID)
                                        });
                                    }, function (err) {
                                        console.log('failed to get the entity status: ' + err);
                                    });
                            }));
                        }
                        Promise.all(arrayOfPromises)
                            .then(function (finalResponse) {
                                resolve(finalResponse);
                            });

                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        reject(err);
                    })
                });
            }
        };

        window.addEventListener('load', function () {
            document.querySelectorAll(".sso-institution").forEach(function (institution) {
                var entityId = institution.getAttribute('data-entityid');
                var entityName = institution.getAttribute('data-name');
                var entitydata = {
                    entityID: entityId,
                    title: entityName
                };
                institution.addEventListener("click", function (e) {
                    e.preventDefault();
                    var self = this;
                    SeamlessAccessService.updateEntity(entitydata).then(function (res) {
                        console.log(res);
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    }).catch(function (err){
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    });
                });
            });
        });

    </script>

   <div class="abstract-group ">
      <section class="article-section article-section__abstract" lang="en" data-lang="en" lang-name="English" id="section-1-en">
         <h2 id="d240405183" class="article-section__header section__title main abstractlang_en main">Abstract</h2>
         <div class="article-section__content en main">
            
            <p>Transition metal selenides (TMSes) are considered promising candidates for the anodes of sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) due to their substantial theoretical capacity. However, TMSes still face with inferior cycling lifespan caused by sluggish Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion kinetics and vigorous volume variations during dis/charge processes. Engineering heterostructure is an attractive solution for rapid Na<sup>+</sup> transfer, and introducing carbonaceous materials also facilitates enhanced conductivity and structural stability. Herein, CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub> heterostructure combined with homogeneous carbon composites are rational designed. The kinetic analysis and theoretical calculations verified that heterointerface engineering induced build-in electric field effect can amplifies the Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion kinetics, while carbon contributes to enhanced electrical conductivity and structural stability. Expectedly, the CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C exhibits high capacity and extremely ultra-long lifespan (320.9&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 2.0&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> over 10,000 cycles with an average decay of only 0.01781&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> per cycle). Furthermore, in situ X-ray diffraction&nbsp;(XRD), ex situ X-ray photoelectorn (XPS), and high-resolution electron microscopy (HRTEM)&nbsp;are exploited to explore the Na<sup>+</sup> storage mechanism. In addition, the Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>@rGO//CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C (NVP@rGO//CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C) pouch-type full-cells are successfully assembled and delivered satisfactory performance. This research presents a viable strategy for the targeted engineering of TMSes aimed at enhancing the efficiency of SIBs.</p>
            </div>
      </section>
   </div>
   <div class="pb-dropzone" data-pb-dropzone="below-abstract-group"><!-- Empty dropzone --></div>
   
   <section class="article-section article-section__full">
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adfm202406915-sec-0010">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adfm202406915-sec-0010-title">1 Introduction</h2>
         
         <p>Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have been considered as promising and competitive alternation/supplements for lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) owing to their low cost, plentiful sodium resources, chemical reaction mechanisms that analogous to those of LIBs, and the redox potential of sodium is just 0.3&nbsp;V higher than that of lithium, positioning them as promising contenders for advanced rechargeable energy storage solutions.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0001" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0001_R_d240405175e477" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 1 - Green Energy Resour.">1</a>-<a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0003" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0003_R_d240405175e477" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 3 - Acc. Chem. Res.">3</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> However, the sluggish Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion kinetics and serious volume expansion in the anodes caused by the Na<sup>+</sup> radius is much more substantial than that of Li<sup>+</sup> result in undesirable sodium storage performance, including poor cycling life and rate capability, which limits the development and application of SIBs.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0004" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0004_R_d240405175e489" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 4 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.">4</a>-<a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0007" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0007_R_d240405175e489" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 7 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">7</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Therefore, exploring appropriate anode materials with accelerated reaction kinetics and enhanced structural stability through rational design and controllable preparation, is believed to be vital approach to achieve the application of SIBs.</p>
         
         <p>Transition metal selenides (TMSes) have attracted significant attention so far for their high theoretical capacity, positioning them as promising anode materials for SIBs.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0008" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0008_R_d240405175e497" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 8 - Small">8</a>, <a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0009" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0009_R_d240405175e497" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 9 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">9</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In comparison to transition metal sulfides, TMSes possess relatively weaker metal-Se bond strengths and enhanced conductivity, promoting the insertion/extraction of Na<sup>+</sup>.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0010" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0010_R_d240405175e504" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 10 - Chem. Eng. J.">10</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In particular, MoSe<sub>2</sub> has been widely explored because of its typical layered structure with large interlayer spacing (0.64&nbsp;nm) and small bandgap, which facilitates the transport of Na<sup>+</sup>.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0011" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0011_R_d240405175e514" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 11 - Carbon">11</a>, <a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0012" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0012_R_d240405175e514" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 12 - Adv. Sci.">12</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> CoSe anodes show high theoretical specific capacity (&gt;300&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0013" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0013_R_d240405175e522" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 13 - Nanoscale">13</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Although MoSe<sub>2</sub> and CoSe have been identified as promising candidate materials for SIBs, the relatively modest inherent electronic conductivity of these materials continues to impede the kinetics of the Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion reaction, and the structural instability caused by huge volume variation induced by Na<sup>+</sup> insertion and extraction, leading to inferior cycle stability and rate capability.</p>
         
         <p>To address the issues mentioned earlier, various schemes have been put forward to enhance the electrical conductivity and structural integrity of CoSe and MoSe<sub>2</sub> based anode materials. Controlling morphology and introducing carbonaceous material are most common approaches to alleviate the volumetric variation and enhance the electrical conductivity of CoSe and MoSe<sub>2</sub>. Huang et&nbsp;al.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0014" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0014_R_d240405175e540" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 14 - Appl. Surf. Sci.">14</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> embedded CoSe nanoparticles into honeycomb carbon nanorods (CoSe@HPCNF), where the honeycomb porous carbon can enhance cycling stability and improve electronic conductivity, and the CoSe@HPCNF delivers improved cycling stability. Yousaf et&nbsp;al.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0015" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0015_R_d240405175e545" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 15 - Adv. Energy Mater.">15</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> encapsulated MoSe<sub>2</sub> on carbon nanotubes (CNTs) and further encapsulated carbon in layers to form CNT/MoSe<sub>2</sub>/C nanotubes. The synergistic effect between the dual carbon network and the enlarged MoSe<sub>2</sub> layer spacing yielded an excellent sodium storage performances. However, the charge transfer within electrode material has still not been improved effectively. Recently, the construction of heterostructure has been an effective approach to facilitate internal ion/electron transport.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0016" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0016_R_d240405175e557" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 16 - Adv. Mater. Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.">16</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Moreover, the bimetallic selenide heterostructure combines the advantages of each component and also features a variety of redox reactions, as well as multimetallic synergistic effect.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0017" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0017_R_d240405175e563" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 17 - Small">17</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Meanwhile, heterostructure with phase interface can easily generate rich lattice defects, which can provide more ion transport channels and active sites, further enhancing ion adsorption energy and improving ion diffusion kinetics.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0018" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0018_R_d240405175e568" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 18 - Small">18</a>-<a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0020" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0020_R_d240405175e568" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 20 - Adv. Mater.">20</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> For instance, the improved electrochemical performance of the CoSe<sub>2</sub>/WSe<sub>2</sub> heterostructure was originated from the introduction of a built-in electric field.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0021" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0021_R_d240405175e578" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 21 - Small">21</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The superior rate capability of the ZnSe/CoSe<sub>2</sub> is mainly due to the significantly improved Na<sup>+</sup>/electron diffusion kinetics of the heterostructure.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0022" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0022_R_d240405175e587" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 22 - Small">22</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Moreover, introducing carbon materials internally while constructing heterostructure is expected to achieve a synergistic improvement in structural stability and ion transport kinetics.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0022" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0022_R_d240405175e593" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 22 - Small">22</a>, <a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0023" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0023_R_d240405175e593" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 23 - Chem. Eng. J. Chem. Eng. J.">23</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> For example, capping carbon on the surface of CoSe<sub>2</sub>-Cu<sub>2</sub>Se nanospheres can inhibit volume expansion, prevent particle agglomeration, and improve structural integrity during the reaction process.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0023" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0023_R_d240405175e602" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 23 - Chem. Eng. J. Chem. Eng. J.">23</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <p>Herein, we have designed a CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C nanosphere heterostructure via facile solvothermal process, and simultaneous selenization and carbonization strategies. The CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C anode has the following prominent superiorities: 1) The heterostructure combines the advantages of both CoSe and MoSe<sub>2</sub> simultaneously, which is favorable for sodium ion storage. 2) The construction of heterostructure could reorganize the heterointerface charge distribution and generate an internal electric field, which would significantly lower the ion diffusion energy barrier and thus enabling rapid charge transfer. 3) The carbon derived from glycerol at high temperature is uniformly dispersed in heterostructure materials, aiding in the enhancement of electronic conductivity and the reduction of volume fluctuations in CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C. Consequently, benefiting from these merits, the CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C heterostructure anode exhibits superior ultralong lifespan (320.3&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> up to 10000 cycles at 2.0&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>) and impressive rate performance (230.0&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 10.0&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>). Furthermore, in situ X-ray diffraction (XRD), ex situ X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS), ex situ high-resolution electron microscopy (HRTEM) techniques, and density functional theory (DFT) calculations elucidate the intricate mechanism behind the enhanced Na<sup>+</sup> storage performance. Moreover, the Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>@rGO//CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C pouch-type full-cells were effectively integrated and powered a light bulb, indicating promising potentials for practical applications.</p>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adfm202406915-sec-0020">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adfm202406915-sec-0020-title">2 Results and Discussion</h2>
         
         <p><b>Scheme</b>&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406915-fig-0009">1</a> illustrates the schematic representation of the fabrication process and crystal structure of the CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C heterostructure. Initially, CoMo-glycerate nanospheres were fabricated using a simple solvothermal method, and then converted into CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C heterostructure through the selenization process. Meanwhile, the amorphous carbon derived from glycerol at high temperatures uniformly distributed in the heterostructure. The inherent electric field created spontaneously at the heterojunction interface of CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub> is contributed to accelerated internal charge transfer, and the uniformly distributed carbon in heterostructure further enhance external charge transfer and structural stability, leading to improved Na<sup>+</sup> storage performance of CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C anode.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202406915-fig-0009"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/f1c4da37-d295-4b17-8716-06307382c39a/adfm202406915-fig-0009-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/f1c4da37-d295-4b17-8716-06307382c39a/adfm202406915-fig-0009-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/df41ec76-7f57-4925-a004-7d5edf1258f7/adfm202406915-fig-0009-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/f1c4da37-d295-4b17-8716-06307382c39a/adfm202406915-fig-0009-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Scheme 1<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202406915-fig-0009&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202406915" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">The manufacture schematic illustration of the CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C heterostructure.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>The phase and crystallinity of the synthesized products were analyzed using XRD. <b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406915-fig-0001">1a</a> presents the XRD patterns of CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C, CoSe-C, and MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C, in which it is clear that the peaks locate at 33.19°, 44.81°, 50.37°, 62.10°, and 69.68° can be well assigned to the (101), (102), (110), and (112) indices of CoSe (JCPDS card No. 70–2870). While the peaks at 13. 69°, 31.42°, 37.88°, and 55.91° belong to the (002), (100), (103), and (110) indices of MoSe<sub>2</sub> (JCPDS card No. 29–0914), respectively.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0024" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0024_R_d240405175e703" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 24 - Adv. Mater.">24</a>, <a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0025" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0025_R_d240405175e703" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 25 - Adv. Mater. Chem. Eng. J. J. Mater. Chem. A">25</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Nevertheless, the diffraction intensities of (002) peaks for MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C and CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C locate at 13.69° are weaker and broader than those of the related MoSe<sub>2</sub> materials in reported literatures, which could be attributed to the destruction of van der Waals forces by the glycerate-derived carbon, thereby diminishing the layer stacking of MoSe<sub>2</sub>, augmenting the space between layers, and leading to the decreased particle size.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0025" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0025_R_d240405175e717" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 25 - Adv. Mater. Chem. Eng. J. J. Mater. Chem. A">25</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The diffraction peaks of CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C heterostructure are matched well with CoSe and MoSe<sub>2</sub>, indicating the successfully construction and high purity of heterojunction. Typical crystal structures of CoSe with and MoSe<sub>2</sub> both with hexagonal phase are illustrated schematically in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406915-fig-0001">1b</a>. The diffraction peaks of amorphous carbon are not prominently observable due to the amorphous nature and relatively low amount. The CoMo-glycerate precursors also show no obvious diffraction peaks (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1</a>, Supporting Information). Additionally, Raman spectrum was utilized as evidence to demonstrate the involvement of carbon within the CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C heterostructure (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406915-fig-0001">1c</a>), where the peaks at 1343 and 1583&nbsp;cm<sup>−1</sup> could belong to the characteristic D and G bands of carbon, respectively.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0026" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0026_R_d240405175e742" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 26 - Adv. Energy Mater.">26</a>, <a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0027" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0027_R_d240405175e742" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 27 - Small">27</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In addition, the vibration peaks centered at 235.5, 282.7, and 350&nbsp;cm<sup>−1</sup> belong to the A<sub>1g</sub>, E<sup>1</sup><sub>2</sub><sub>g</sub> and B<sup>1</sup><sub>2g</sub> vibrational mode of MoSe<sub>2</sub>,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0012" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0012_R_d240405175e762" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 12 - Adv. Sci.">12</a>, <a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0028" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0028_R_d240405175e762" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 28 - J. Power Sources Chem. Eng. J.">28</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> and the peak at 670&nbsp;cm<sup>−1</sup> belongs to the A<sub>1g</sub> vibrational mode of CoSe.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0029" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0029_R_d240405175e772" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 29 - Small Chem. Eng. J. J. Power Sources">29</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The surface composition and elemental valence states of the CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C heterojunction were scrutinized using XPS. Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S2</a> (Supporting Information) reveals the presence of Co, Mo, Se, and C elements in the survey spectrum. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406915-fig-0001">1d</a> presents the Co 2p spectrum, where the peaks at 781.0 and 796.3&nbsp;eV are likely indicative of the Co 2p<sub>3/2</sub> and Co 2p<sub>1/2</sub> binding energies for Co<sup>2+</sup>, respectively. Similarly, the peaks at 777.6 and 792.8&nbsp;eV correlated to the Co 2p<sub>3/2</sub> and Co 2p<sub>1/2</sub> for Co<sup>3+</sup> may be attributed to surface oxidation effects.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0018" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0018_R_d240405175e799" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 18 - Small">18</a>, <a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0021" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0021_R_d240405175e799" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 21 - Small">21</a>, <a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0030" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0030_R_d240405175e799" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 30 - Energy Storage Mater.">30</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The peaks situated at 784.8 and 801.5&nbsp;eV correspond to satellite peaks.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0031" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0031_R_d240405175e804" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 31 - Chem. Eng. J.">31</a>, <a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0032" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0032_R_d240405175e804" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 32 - Nano Res.">32</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The Mo 3d spectrum (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406915-fig-0001">1e</a>) exhibits two prominent peaks at 227.8 and 231.1&nbsp;eV, representing Mo 3d<sub>5/2</sub> and Mo 3d<sub>3/2</sub> binding energies characteristic of Mo<sup>4+</sup>.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0033" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0033_R_d240405175e819" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 33 - Small">33</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Furthermore, the minor hump observed at 235.0&nbsp;eV is indicative of the Mo<sup>6+</sup> oxidation state present in MoO<sub>3</sub>, which generate from the oxidation of Mo<sup>4+</sup> on the surface.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0028" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0028_R_d240405175e831" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 28 - J. Power Sources Chem. Eng. J.">28</a>, <a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0034" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0034_R_d240405175e831" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 34 - ACS Appl. Energy Mater.">34</a>, <a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0035" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0035_R_d240405175e831" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 35 - Adv. Mater.">35</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The Se 3d spectrum is presented in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406915-fig-0001">1f</a>, with the peaks at 53.47, 54.26, and 58.5&nbsp;eV corresponding to the Se 3d<sub>5/2</sub>, Se 3d<sub>3/2</sub>, and Se-O binding energies, respectively.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0021" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0021_R_d240405175e844" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 21 - Small">21</a>, <a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0036" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0036_R_d240405175e844" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 36 - ACS Nano">36</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202406915-fig-0001"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/587d7c16-cdea-42c4-9c69-77be0cc3bf45/adfm202406915-fig-0001-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/587d7c16-cdea-42c4-9c69-77be0cc3bf45/adfm202406915-fig-0001-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/6b847703-fbef-4d5c-9cef-6466cca0c986/adfm202406915-fig-0001-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/587d7c16-cdea-42c4-9c69-77be0cc3bf45/adfm202406915-fig-0001-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 1<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202406915-fig-0001&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202406915" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) XRD patterns and b) crystal structures of CoSe and MoSe<sub>2</sub>. c) Raman spectrum, and XPS spectra of d) Co 2p, e) Mo 3d, f) Se 3d of CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>The architecture of the synthesized products were scrutinized using scanning electron microscopy (SEM) and TEM. <b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406915-fig-0002">2a,b</a> and Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S3</a> (Supporting Information) illustrate that the CoMo-glycerate precursor exhibits a uniform nanosphere morphology with smooth surface, and the diameter is ≈500&nbsp;nm. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406915-fig-0002">2c,d</a> and Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S4</a> (Supporting Information) show the typical TEM and SEM images of CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C, it is obviously observed that they basically inherited the original nanospherical morphology of precursor after the selenization and carbonization processes, while the surface became loose and rough. HRTEM image of CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C are presented in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406915-fig-0002">2e</a>, the lattice spacing of 0.645&nbsp;nm observed is consistent with the (002) plane of MoSe<sub>2</sub>, and the lattice spacings measuring 0.241, 0.212, and 0.269&nbsp;nm correspond to the (002), (101), and (102) crystal planes of CoSe, respectively.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0037" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0037_R_d240405175e900" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 37 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">37</a>, <a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0038" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0038_R_d240405175e900" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 38 - Adv. Energy Mater.">38</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Significantly, a clear phase boundary is discernible, which suggests the successful creation of a CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub> heterojunction at the interface. The local built-in electric field could be spontaneously established within the heterojunction interface, which would accelerate internal charge transfer.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0039" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0039_R_d240405175e908" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 39 - Energy Storage Mater.">39</a>, <a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0040" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0040_R_d240405175e908" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 40 - Chem. Eng. J.">40</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406915-fig-0002">2f,g</a> shows the HRTEM image of CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C heterostructure and the corresponding lattice distance curves produced after Fourier transforming the lattice, where the (102) plane of CoSe and the (002) plane of MoSe<sub>2</sub> are further interpreted viscerally. The selected area electron diffraction (SAED) pattern is clearly identified (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406915-fig-0002">2h</a>), two diffraction rings marked with red color are matched to the (101), (102) planes of CoSe, while three diffraction rings with blue color can be indexed to the (002), (103), (110) planes of MoSe<sub>2</sub>, aligning with the findings in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406915-fig-0002">2e</a>. Furthermore, the elemental mappings of the heterojunction obtained through energy-dispersive X-ray spectroscopy (EDX) (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406915-fig-0002">2i</a>) validate the homogeneous distribution of Co, Mo, Se, and C elements, and the SEM-EDX results (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S7a</a>, Supporting Information) indicate the content of CoSe and MoSe<sub>2</sub> in heterostructure is ≈1:1. In addition, the SEM images and corresponding EDX elemental distributions of CoSe and MoSe<sub>2</sub> are shown in Figures&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S5</a> and&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S6</a> (Supporting Information) and Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S7a,b</a> (Supporting Information), and the analysis results indicate that the CoSe displays similar morphology with the CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C heterostructure, while MoSe<sub>2</sub> shows irregular nanospherical structure. The ICP-OES analysis results of the CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C material reveal that the proportion of CoSe and MoSe<sub>2</sub> is ≈11:9 (Table&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1</a>, Supporting Information).</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202406915-fig-0002"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/02c623f5-b7b9-4a55-9f58-21f2589d0c65/adfm202406915-fig-0002-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/02c623f5-b7b9-4a55-9f58-21f2589d0c65/adfm202406915-fig-0002-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/a2caabba-f1d5-44dd-9745-78fdccd1904e/adfm202406915-fig-0002-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/02c623f5-b7b9-4a55-9f58-21f2589d0c65/adfm202406915-fig-0002-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 2<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202406915-fig-0002&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202406915" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) SEM and b) TEM image of CoMo-glycerate precursor. c) SEM, d) TEM, e,f) HRTEM images and g) the lattice distance curves produced after Fourier transforming the lattice, h) SAED pattern and i) EDX elemental mappings of CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C heterostructure.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>CV assessments were employed to probe into the behaviors of Na<sup>+</sup> storage. <b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406915-fig-0003">3a</a> displays the CV curves of the CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C anode with the scan rate of 0.1&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup> over a potential range from 0.3 to 3.0&nbsp;V. During the initial cathodic scan, a subtle peak at 1.05&nbsp;V is detected, potentially corresponding to the formation of Na<sub>x</sub>CoSe and Na<sub>x</sub>MoSe<sub>2</sub> due to the intercalation of Na<sup>+</sup> between the layers of CoSe and MoSe<sub>2</sub>. (CoSe + xNa<sup>+</sup> + xe<sup>−</sup> → Na<sub>x</sub>CoSe; MoSe<sub>2</sub> + xNa<sup>+</sup> + xe<sup>−</sup> → Na<sub>x</sub>MoSe<sub>2</sub>).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0014" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0014_R_d240405175e1028" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 14 - Appl. Surf. Sci.">14</a>, <a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0041" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0041_R_d240405175e1028" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 41 - J. Mater. Chem. A">41</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The cathodic peaks observed at 0.96 and 0.81&nbsp;V are indicative of the transformation process during which Na<sub>x</sub>CoSe is converted into Co and Na<sub>2</sub>Se (Na<sub>x</sub>CoSe + (2-x) Na<sup>+</sup>+ (2-x) e<sup>−</sup> → Co + Na<sub>2</sub>Se), which also accompanied with the development of solid electrolyte interface (SEI) layer.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0014" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0014_R_d240405175e1046" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 14 - Appl. Surf. Sci.">14</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The 0.59&nbsp;V peak in the profile denotes the point at which Na<sub>x</sub>MoSe<sub>2</sub> undergoes a conversion with Na<sup>+</sup>, leading to the production of Mo and Na<sub>2</sub>Se (Na<sub>x</sub>MoSe<sub>2</sub> + (4-x) Na<sup>+</sup>+ (4-x) e<sup>−</sup> → Mo + 2Na<sub>2</sub>Se).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0015" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0015_R_d240405175e1071" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 15 - Adv. Energy Mater.">15</a>, <a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0042" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0042_R_d240405175e1071" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 42 - Small">42</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In the initial anodic scan, a pair of distinct peaks emerged at 1.74 and 1.86&nbsp;V, which are indicative of the respective formations of MoSe<sub>2</sub> and CoSe.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0014" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0014_R_d240405175e1079" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 14 - Appl. Surf. Sci.">14</a>, <a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0015" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0015_R_d240405175e1079" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 15 - Adv. Energy Mater.">15</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> During the subsequent cycles, the anodic peaks show no significant positional shift, while the cathodic peaks show significant shift. The 1.45&nbsp;V cathodic peak is associated with the intercalation and transformation processes of MoSe<sub>2</sub>.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0012" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0012_R_d240405175e1086" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 12 - Adv. Sci.">12</a>, <a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0033" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0033_R_d240405175e1086" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 33 - Small">33</a>, <a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0043" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0043_R_d240405175e1086" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 43 - Small">43</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The formation of Na<sub>x</sub>CoSe is indicated by peaks at 1.18 and 1.33&nbsp;V, whereas the peak at 0.76&nbsp;V corresponds to the production of Na<sub>2</sub>Se and Co.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0014" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0014_R_d240405175e1096" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 14 - Appl. Surf. Sci.">14</a>, <a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0041" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0041_R_d240405175e1096" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 41 - J. Mater. Chem. A">41</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Significantly, the subsequent CV curves exhibit a high degree of overlap, which attests to the excellent reversibility of the CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C electrode. The analysis results of cyclic voltammetry (CV) curves for the individual CoSe and MoSe<sub>2</sub> electrodes in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S8</a> (Supporting Information), are conformed to that of CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C electrode.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202406915-fig-0003"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/aca57f35-d9c3-4054-b65a-f1c5fd6b21f2/adfm202406915-fig-0003-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/aca57f35-d9c3-4054-b65a-f1c5fd6b21f2/adfm202406915-fig-0003-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/23fb8810-8cc9-4b78-a4be-d01cab546e44/adfm202406915-fig-0003-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/aca57f35-d9c3-4054-b65a-f1c5fd6b21f2/adfm202406915-fig-0003-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 3<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202406915-fig-0003&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202406915" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) CV curves at scan rate of 0.1&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup> and b) charge–discharge profiles for 1, 2, 3, 10th, and 20th cycles at 0.2&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. c) Cycling performances at 0.5&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, d) charge–discharge profiles at different current densities, e) rate performance and f,g) long cycling performances at 2.0 and 3.0&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406915-fig-0003">3b</a> presents the charge/discharge profiles of the CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C at 0.2&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, in which the working voltage platforms are correspond well to the CV curve results. Clearly, the initial discharge and charge specific capacities are recorded as 532.0 and 394.4&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, respectively, corresponding to a high coulombic efficiency (CE) of 74.14%. The not recoverable capacity may be associated with the development of the SEI layer, as well as a few irreversible reactions.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0011" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0011_R_d240405175e1151" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 11 - Carbon">11</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> During the initial 1000 cycles, the CE is up to ≈100% and the capacity is virtually undecayed (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S9</a>, Supporting Information), indicating the well structure integrity of CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C electrode during electrochemical processes. In contrast, CoSe and MoSe<sub>2</sub> have worse cycling stability at 0.2&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S10</a>, Supporting Information). As depicted in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406915-fig-0003">3c</a>, which represents the cycling performance at a current density of 0.5&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, the CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C electrode demonstrates an elevated initial discharge capacity of 453.1&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, surpassing the capacities of the CoSe-C (421.3&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>) and MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C (355.4&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>) electrodes. All the electrodes exhibit a phenomena of certain capacity decay over the proceeding cycles, which can be ascribed to the gradual activation of electrodes, the occurrence of side reactions and the development of the SEI film.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0044" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0044_R_d240405175e1186" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 44 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">44</a>, <a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0045" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0045_R_d240405175e1186" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 45 - Adv. Mater. Adv. Funct. Mater. Adv. Funct. Mater.">45</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C electrode delivers a charge/discharge capacities of 368.8/369.9&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 2000 cycles, while the capacities of CoSe and MoSe<sub>2</sub> electrodes are only 257.9/256.5 and 287.6/286.5&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 850 and 770 cycles, respectively. In addition, the rate properties of CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406915-fig-0003">3d</a> indicate that the voltage plateaus at different current densities are almost at the same position, which demonstrate the favorable reversibility of the CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406915-fig-0003">3e</a> demonstrates that the CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C shows an average specific discharge capacities of 380.3, 360.9, 344.8, 327.7, 304.5, and 273.1&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at various current densities. Even at 10&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, its average discharge capacity is maintained at 230&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. Upon reverting to 0.1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after undergoing two of the above cycles, the discharge capacity holds strong at 294.7&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. In contrast, CoSe and MoSe<sub>2</sub> both show poor rate performances (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S11</a>, Supporting Information). Moreover, the CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C material still maintains nanospherical morphology after cycling (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S12</a>, Supporting Information), which further verify the structural stability of the heterostructure.</p>
         
         <p>The performances of the electrodes over prolonged periods of operation at high rates were evaluated, and all electrodes underwent initial 5-cycle activation phase at 0.5&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406915-fig-0003">3f</a> illustrates the cycling stability at 2.0&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, in which the CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C electrode deliver a stable specific capacities of 319.9/320.3&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> over 10000 cycles, with a minimal average capacity decay of just 0.01781&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> per cycle, while the CoSe-C and MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C only maintain specific capacities of 257.0/256.7 and 286.3/286.8&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 6500 and 1500 cycles, respectively. Similarly, CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C maintains superior specific capacity and enhanced cycling stability compared to CoSe-C and MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C at 1.0&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> (Figures&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S13</a> and&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S14</a>, Supporting Information). Even when tested under 3.0&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406915-fig-0003">3g</a>), CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C maintains extremely long lifespan (retaining specific capacities of 250.1/249.8&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> across an extensive 16000 cycles), which displays a more favorable electrochemical performance compared to CoSe-C and MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C, demonstrating that the heterostructure construction facilitates the acceleration of Na<sup>+</sup> reaction kinetics, and buffers the volumetric variation. Besides, the uniformly distributed carbon could hinder the agglomeration of the CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub> heterostructure. In addition, as illustrated in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S15</a> (Supporting Information), the Na<sup>+</sup> storage performance of CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C electrode was tested within a discharge cutoff voltage of 0.01&nbsp;V in ether-based electrolyte, while the electrode delivers poor cycling stability, which might be ascribed to the severe volume expansion caused by the deep discharging process.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0045" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0045_R_d240405175e1292" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 45 - Adv. Mater. Adv. Funct. Mater. Adv. Funct. Mater.">45</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In addition, the electrochemical performance of CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C electrode in a carbonate-based electrolyte within a voltage range from 0.3 to 3.0&nbsp;V has been further explored (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S16</a>, Supporting Information), and the electrode also presents poor performance. The comparative findings from these tests consistently demonstrate that the CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C electrode possesses a distinct advantage in terms of cycling stability when it is used in conjunction with an ether-based electrolyte, particularly within the voltage range of 0.3 to 3.0&nbsp;V.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0045" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0045_R_d240405175e1305" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 45 - Adv. Mater. Adv. Funct. Mater. Adv. Funct. Mater.">45</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Based on our understanding, the CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C electrode exhibits notable advantages over other previously reported selenide-based materials (Table&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S2</a>, Supporting Information).</p>
         
         <div class="paragraph-element">To investigate the reaction dynamics characters of the electrodes, galvanostatic intermittent titration technique (GITT) curves were employed (<b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406915-fig-0004">4a</a>). Specifically, the voltage behavior is closely examined when the electrode undergoes a single current pulse at 0.02&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> for a duration of 1200&nbsp;s, followed by an open-circuit rest period of 7200&nbsp;s (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S17</a>, Supporting Information). The diffusion coefficient for sodium ions (<i>D</i><sub>Na</sub><sup>+</sup>) is determinable through the following equation:<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0046" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0046_R_d240405175e1334" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 46 - Small">46</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup>
            
            <div class="inline-equation" id="adfm202406915-disp-0001"><span class="inline-equation__construct"><!--FIGURE-->

                        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">$$\begin{equation}{{D}_{{\mathrm{N}}{{{\mathrm{a}}}^{\mathrm{ + }}}}}{\mathrm{ = }}\frac{{\mathrm{4}}}{{{\mathrm{\pi \tau }}}}\ {{\left( {\frac{{m{{V}_{\mathrm{m}}}}}{{MA}}} \right)}^{\mathrm{2}}}{{\left( {\frac{{{{\Delta}}{{E}_{\mathrm{s}}}}}{{{{\Delta}}{{E}_{{\tau}}}}}} \right)}^{\mathrm{2}}}\end{equation}$$</annotation>
                     </semantics></math></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(1)</span></div>where <i>τ</i> represents the duration of the pulse, <i>m</i>, <i>V</i><sub>m</sub>, and <i>M</i> denote the mass, molar volume, and molar mass of the active material, respectively. <i>A</i> represents the electrode area. Δ<i>E</i><sub>s</sub> represents the change in voltage during the equilibrium state, occurring prior to and following the current pulse, and Δ<i>E</i><sub>τ</sub> refers to the voltage change caused by the constant current charge/discharge processes. The respective <i>D</i><sub>Na</sub><sup>+</sup> for the CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C, CoSe-C, and MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C electrodes are depicted in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406915-fig-0004">4b,c</a>, respectively. The analyses indicate that the CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C electrode (10<sup>–9</sup>–10<sup>−12</sup>&nbsp;cm<sup>2</sup>&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup>) exhibits a higher range of <i>D</i><sub>Na</sub><sup>+</sup> compared to the CoSe-C (10<sup>−10</sup>–10<sup>−13</sup>&nbsp;cm<sup>2</sup>&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup>) and MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C (10<sup>−10.5</sup>–10<sup>−13</sup>&nbsp;cm<sup>2</sup>&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup>) electrodes, implying the heterostructure engineering is beneficial for enhancing the Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion kinetics.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0047" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0047_R_d240405175e1463" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 47 - Adv. Energy Mater.">47</a>, <a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0048" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0048_R_d240405175e1463" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 48 - Adv. Energy Mater. Adv. Mater. Adv. Funct. Mater.">48</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> It is worth noting that the <i>D</i><sub>Na</sub><sup>+</sup> decreases significantly near 1.75&nbsp;V, which might be attributed to the progresses of conversion reaction.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0048" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0048_R_d240405175e1472" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 48 - Adv. Energy Mater. Adv. Mater. Adv. Funct. Mater.">48</a></sup></span><sup>-</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0048" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0048_R_d240405175e1476" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 48 - Adv. Energy Mater. Adv. Mater. Adv. Funct. Mater.">48</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Moreover, the CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C also displays lower reaction resistance than that of CoSe-C and MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C electrodes in both charge and discharge processes (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406915-fig-0004">4d,e</a>), further indicating the prominent advantages of heterostructure.</div>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202406915-fig-0004"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/5fef3f7f-89c0-4952-9c3b-839c7d81d7a7/adfm202406915-fig-0004-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/5fef3f7f-89c0-4952-9c3b-839c7d81d7a7/adfm202406915-fig-0004-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/18e33e66-3645-4887-8a53-8b3866bfc7f6/adfm202406915-fig-0004-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/5fef3f7f-89c0-4952-9c3b-839c7d81d7a7/adfm202406915-fig-0004-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 4<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202406915-fig-0004&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202406915" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) GITT curves, and corresponding Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion coefficient during b) charge and c) discharge processes, and the relation between capacity and reaction resistance during d) charge and e) discharge processes. f) Nyquist plots before cycling, g) after 10 cycles and the corresponding equivalent circuit and h) the plots of <i>Z</i>' versus <i>ω</i><sup>−1/2</sup> in fresh and after 10 cycles.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <div class="paragraph-element">The electrodes underwent electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (EIS) to have their electrochemical impedance characteristics assessed. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406915-fig-0004">4f,g</a> present the Nyquist plots for the anodes both prior to and after 10 cycles, along with their respective fitted equivalent circuit diagrams. The Nyquist plots indicate that the semicircle present in the high-frequency region corresponds to the charge transfer resistance (<i>R</i><sub>ct</sub>), and the diagonal line indicates the Warburg resistance (<i>W</i><sub>0</sub>), associated with the diffusion of Na<sup>+</sup>.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0049" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0049_R_d240405175e1531" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 49 - Chem. Eng. J.">49</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> It is demonstrated that CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C has lower <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> values than those of CoSe-C and MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C both before and after cycling, and the <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> values of the electrodes both decreased after cycling, suggesting formtion of stable SEI without repeated fracture and regeneration.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0050" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0050_R_d240405175e1547" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 50 - Small">50</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Moreover, the <i>D</i><sub>Na</sub><sup>+</sup> also could be calculated as following Equations:<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0021" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0021_R_d240405175e1557" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 21 - Small">21</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup>
            
            <div class="inline-equation" id="adfm202406915-disp-0002"><span class="inline-equation__construct"><!--FIGURE-->
                  <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/8b6838e3-457e-4c05-935d-5d7624ede15c/adfm202406915-math-0002.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:1616301X:media:adfm202406915:adfm202406915-math-0002" display="block" location="graphic/adfm202406915-math-0002.png">
                     <semantics>

                              <mrow>
                                 <mi>Na</mi>
                                 <mo>+</mo>
                              </mrow>
                           </msub>
                           <mo linebreak="badbreak">=</mo>
                           <mn>0.5</mn>
                           <mspace width="0.33em"></mspace>
                           <msup>
                              <mrow>
                                 <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>

                                 <mi>A</mi>
                                 <msup>
                                    <mi>n</mi>
                                    <mn>2</mn>
                                 </msup>
                                 <msup>

                                 </msup>

                              </mrow>

                           </msup>
                        </mrow>
                        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">$$\begin{equation}D_{\mathrm{Na +}} = 0.5\ (RT{\mathrm{/}}An^{\mathrm{2}}F^{\mathrm{2}}C\sigma )^2\end{equation}$$</annotation>
                     </semantics></math></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(2)</span></div>
            <div class="inline-equation" id="adfm202406915-disp-0003"><span class="inline-equation__construct"><!--FIGURE-->
                  <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/d2b8539f-3a04-4f11-bfa5-6e0cc1ac1350/adfm202406915-math-0003.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:1616301X:media:adfm202406915:adfm202406915-math-0003" display="block" location="graphic/adfm202406915-math-0003.png">

                           </msub>
                           <mo linebreak="badbreak">+</mo>
                           <msub>
                              <mi>R</mi>
                              <mi>ct</mi>
                           </msub>
                           <mo linebreak="goodbreak">+</mo>
                           <mi>σ</mi>
                           <msup>
