                                 <mn>1</mn>
                                 <mo>/</mo>
                                 <mn>2</mn>
                              </mrow>
                           </msup>
                        </mrow>
                        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">$$\begin{equation}Z{\mathrm{^{\prime}\ = \ }}R_{\mathrm{e}} + R_{\mathrm{ct}} + \sigma \omega ^{\mathrm{ - 1/2}}\end{equation}$$</annotation>
                     </semantics></math></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(3)</span></div>where <i>A</i>, <i>n</i>, <i>F</i>, <i>R</i>, <i>T</i>, and <i>C</i> represent the electrode area, the charge transfer number, the Faraday constant, the gas constant, absolute temperature and Na<sup>+</sup> concentration, respectively. <i>σ</i> and <i>ω</i> are Warburg factor and the angular frequency (<i>ω&nbsp;</i>=&nbsp;2<i>πf</i>). According to the above equations, the smaller <i>σ</i> values mean larger <i>D</i><sub>Na</sub><sup>+</sup>. In Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406915-fig-0004">4h</a>, the CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C electrode shows larger <i>D</i><sub>Na</sub><sup>+</sup> than that of CoSe-C and MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C, indicating the fast Na<sup>+</sup> migration rate and reaction kinetics, which might be ascribed to the creation of heterointerfaces within the CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0021" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0021_R_d240405175e1682" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 21 - Small">21</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></div>
         
         <p>To gain a deeper comprehension of the superior Na<sup>+</sup> retention capabilities of the CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C electrode, CV tests are used to infer reaction dynamics. <b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406915-fig-0005">5a–c</a> shows the CV curves for the CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C, MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C, and CoSe-C electrodes at different scan rates. The progressively wider curves with increasing scan rate indicate significant pseudo-capacitive behavior and low polarisation.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0051" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0051_R_d240405175e1704" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 51 - Energy Storage Mater.">51</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Typically, the contribution of pseudo-capacitance can be quantitatively determined by examining the relationship between current (<i>i</i>) on scan rate (<i>v</i>) following the equations: <i>i&nbsp;</i>=&nbsp;<i>av<sup>b</sup></i> and log (<i>i</i>)&nbsp;<i>=&nbsp;</i>log(<i>a</i>) + <i>b</i>log(<i>v</i>). When the <i>b</i> value equals 0.5, it signifies that the process is dominated by diffusion, while <i>b</i> value of 1.0 suggests that the behavior is primarily controlled by pseudocapacitance.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0052" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0052_R_d240405175e1735" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 52 - Nano Today">52</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> As depicted in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406915-fig-0005">5d–f</a>, the <i>b</i>-values are in the range of 0.5–1.0 for three electrodes, indicating that the Na<sup>+</sup> storage reactions are dominated by both diffusion-controlled behavior and pseudocapacitive-controlled behavior. Furthermore, the relative contributions of the diffusion process and pseudocapacitive behavior can be precisely determined using the equation: <i>i</i>(<i>v</i>)&nbsp;=&nbsp;<i>k</i><sub>1</sub><i>v</i> + <i>k</i><sub>2</sub><i>v</i><sup>1/2</sup>, with <i>k</i><sub>1</sub><i>v</i> representing the pseudocapacitive contribution and <i>k</i><sub>2</sub><i>v</i><sup>1/2</sup> representing the diffusion-controlled part.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0053" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0053_R_d240405175e1772" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 53 - Adv. Mater.">53</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The capacitance contribution for the CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C, MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C, and CoSe-C electrodes at 0.8&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup> are 90.2%, 87.1%, and 86.7%, respectively (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406915-fig-0005">5g–i</a>). A high capacitance contribution means faster Na<sup>+</sup> storage kinetics, which is crucial for superior rate performance. The capacitance contributions of CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C, MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C, and CoSe-C at other scan rates are plotted in Figures&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S18</a>–<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S20</a> (Supporting Information). Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406915-fig-0005">5j</a> shows the capacitance contributions of the three electrodes at various scan rates, and the capacitance contribution of the CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C electrode improves considerably over the other two electrodes as the scan rate increases, aligning with its superior rate and cycling characteristics.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0042" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0042_R_d240405175e1805" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 42 - Small">42</a>, <a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0050" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0050_R_d240405175e1805" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 50 - Small">50</a>, <a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0051" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0051_R_d240405175e1805" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 51 - Energy Storage Mater.">51</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202406915-fig-0005"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/c1f3c832-38e4-4736-9b85-5c8855526d07/adfm202406915-fig-0005-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/c1f3c832-38e4-4736-9b85-5c8855526d07/adfm202406915-fig-0005-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/5fc40714-c402-4b87-b744-4ac56d3455b8/adfm202406915-fig-0005-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/c1f3c832-38e4-4736-9b85-5c8855526d07/adfm202406915-fig-0005-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 5<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202406915-fig-0005&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202406915" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a–c) CV curves at various scan rates, and d–f) corresponding log (<i>i</i>) versus log (<i>v</i>) plots. g–i) Normalized contribution ratio at different scan rates at a scan rate of 0.8&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup>. j) Pseudocapacitive contributions.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>To further explore the Na<sup>+</sup> storage mechanism of CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C electrode, in situ XRD, ex situ XRD, Raman, HRTEM, and XPS analyses were performed. <b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406915-fig-0006">6a,b</a> are the results of in situ XRD tests, which can be divided into four steps. During the discharge process (stage I), diffraction peaks that correspond to the (101) and (102) crystal planes of CoSe (JCPDS card No. 70–2870) and the (100) crystal plane of MoSe<sub>2</sub> (JCPDS card No. 29–0914) are noticeable.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0042" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0042_R_d240405175e1851" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 42 - Small">42</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> As the discharge proceeds, CoSe is completely consumed, resulting in the formation of Co and Na<sub>2</sub>Se.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0054" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0054_R_d240405175e1858" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 54 - Small">54</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In the stage II, the (111) and (220) crystal planes of Na<sub>2</sub>Se (JCPDS card No. 65–0524) are observed, which are produced through conversion reaction of CoSe and MoSe<sub>2</sub>. Concurrently, the diffraction peaks of MoSe<sub>2</sub> gradually vanished, indicating that MoSe<sub>2</sub> has been fully transformed into Mo and Na<sub>2</sub>Se. The metallic forms of Mo and Co exhibit low crystallinity, which renders them challenging to identify through detection methods. During the subsequent charging process (stages III and IV), the diffraction peaks of Na<sub>2</sub>Se gradually diminished, indicating that a reversible transformation reaction has taken place. Nonetheless, the resulting MoSe<sub>2</sub> and CoSe from the conversion process exhibit low crystallinity, making their detection elusive.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0026" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0026_R_d240405175e1879" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 26 - Adv. Energy Mater.">26</a>, <a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0055" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0055_R_d240405175e1879" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 55 - Chem. Eng. J.">55</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The initial charge–discharge curves are depicted in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S21a</a> (Supporting Information), with “a” through “j” indicating various voltage stages, and Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S21b</a> (Supporting Information) exhibits the corresponding ex situ XRD patterns. At the open circuit voltage, the diffraction peaks correspond to the CoSe (JCPDS card No. 70–2870) and MoSe<sub>2</sub> (JCPDS card No. 29–0914) phases in sequence. During discharge to 1.7&nbsp;V or even 1.2&nbsp;V, the intensities of the diffraction peaks for both CoSe and MoSe<sub>2</sub> progressively diminish, while no significant peak position changes, corresponding to the processes of Na<sup>+</sup> insertion of CoSe and MoSe<sub>2</sub>, respectively. As the discharge voltage reached 0.9&nbsp;V, a faint peak of metal Co (JCPDS card No. 89–4308) appeared along with the disappeared diffraction peaks of CoSe, implying the occurrence of a reaction that transforms CoSe into Co. As the discharge process continues, the peak of MoSe<sub>2</sub> gradually disappeared, and peaks of Na<sub>2</sub>Se (JCPDS card No. 65–0524) and metal Mo (JCPDS card No. 89–4896) appeared when the discharge reached 0.3&nbsp;V, indicating the conversion reaction of MoSe<sub>2</sub> to Mo. During the charge processes, the diffraction peaks of Co, Mo and Na<sub>2</sub>Se progressively disappeared and some diffraction peaks of CoSe and MoSe<sub>2</sub> phases reappeared after charged to 3.0&nbsp;V. The ex situ Raman spectra analysis (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S22</a>, Supporting Information) further confirmed the reversible generation of MoSe<sub>2</sub> and CoSe.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0028" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0028_R_d240405175e1915" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 28 - J. Power Sources Chem. Eng. J.">28</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202406915-fig-0006"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/37c12184-6b02-40de-a17f-020937f14540/adfm202406915-fig-0006-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/37c12184-6b02-40de-a17f-020937f14540/adfm202406915-fig-0006-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/392bf483-1285-44f6-b8d3-ed90e78b8713/adfm202406915-fig-0006-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/37c12184-6b02-40de-a17f-020937f14540/adfm202406915-fig-0006-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 6<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202406915-fig-0006&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202406915" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) Contour plots and b) stacked patterns of in situ XRD patterns during the initial cycle. XPS spectra of c) Co 2p and d) Mo 3d at different voltage states for the CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C electrode. The ex situ HRTEM after being discharged to e,f) 0.3&nbsp;V, and charged to g,h) 3.0&nbsp;V of CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C electrode. i) Schematic diagram of the sodiation/de-sodiation processes.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>The ex situ XPS analyses were further carried out to investigate the changes in electronic states. The Co 2p spectra are shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406915-fig-0006">6c</a>. At 0.3&nbsp;V, peaks observed at 781.0 and 796.3&nbsp;eV are attributed to Co<sup>0</sup>, suggesting the conversion of CoSe to Co upon full discharge. Upon charging to 3.0&nbsp;V, the peaks of Co<sup>0</sup> vanished, and the peaks aligned with those of the initial state, demonstrating the reversible formation of CoSe.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0056" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0056_R_d240405175e1953" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 56 - Electrochim. Acta">56</a>, <a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0057" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0057_R_d240405175e1953" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 57 - Energy Environ. Mater.">57</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406915-fig-0006">6d</a> shows the Mo 3d spectra, when the electrode discharged to 0.3&nbsp;V, the peaks of Mo<sup>4+</sup> shifted to a lower energy level and the peaks correspond to metallic Mo appeared, indicating that MoSe<sub>2</sub> undergoes a conversion reaction.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0050" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0050_R_d240405175e1966" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 50 - Small">50</a>, <a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0058" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0058_R_d240405175e1966" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 58 - Small">58</a>, <a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0059" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0059_R_d240405175e1966" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 59 - J. Energy Chem.">59</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> During the subsequent charging phase, the signature peaks revert to their original positions, indicating the regeneration of MoSe<sub>2</sub>. Whereas, the appearance of Mo<sup>6+</sup> signal may be due to the slight oxidation of metal Mo and MoSe<sub>2</sub> during the electrochemical reaction as well as the testing process.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0042" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0042_R_d240405175e1978" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 42 - Small">42</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The electronic states change of Se 3d is shown in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S23</a> (Supporting Information), all the peaks shifted slightly to high energy level after fully discharge and charge, which might be related to the conversion of Na<sub>2</sub>Se species during the process of sodiation/de-sodiation processes.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0060" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0060_R_d240405175e1989" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 60 - Adv. Mater.">60</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The ex situ HRTEM images of CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C electrodes were examined to further confirm the Na<sup>+</sup> storage mechanism. Upon initial discharge to 0.3&nbsp;V, the lattice distances of 0.341, 0.222, and 0.205&nbsp;nm were observed, aligning with the Na<sub>2</sub>Se (111) plane, the Mo (110) phase, and the Co (002) plane, respectively. (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406915-fig-0006">6e,f</a>). The HRTEM images at fully charged 3.0&nbsp;V (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406915-fig-0006">6g,h</a>) present the lattice spacings of 0.268 and 0.264&nbsp;nm, which can be indexed to (101) and (002) crystal planes of CoSe, while 0.645 and 0.283&nbsp;nm correlating with (002) and (100) planes of MoSe<sub>2</sub>, respectively. The above analysis results further demonstrate that CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C electrode undergoes the conversion reaction. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406915-fig-0006">6i</a> shows a schematic of the Na<sup>+</sup> storage mechanism of the electrode. The results obtained from the analysis corroborate the patterns observed in CV curves, and preliminary verified the conversion reaction mechanism of CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C.</p>
         
         <p>The density of states (DOS) curves of CoSe, MoSe<sub>2</sub>, and CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub> are illustrated in <b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406915-fig-0007">7a</a>. Within the DOS of the CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub> heterostructure, a noticeable amplification in electron delocalization is observed around the Fermi energy level, and the enhancement might be primarily attributed to the heterointerface.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0026" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0026_R_d240405175e2034" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 26 - Adv. Energy Mater.">26</a>, <a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0061" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0061_R_d240405175e2034" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 61 - Adv. Energy Mater.">61</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406915-fig-0007">7b</a> illustrates a schematic diagram showcasing the Na<sup>+</sup> adsorption sites on CoSe, MoSe<sub>2</sub>, and CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>, with the corresponding adsorption energies for Na<sup>+</sup> are −0.793, −1.729, and −1.891&nbsp;eV (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406915-fig-0007">7c</a>), repsectively. The formation of the CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub> heterostructure increases the Na<sup>+</sup> adsorption energy, which improves the stability of the discharge product anchoring and enhances the reaction kinetics.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406915-bib-0062" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406915-bib-0062_R_d240405175e2058" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 62 - ACS Nano Small">62</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The charge difference distribution for CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub> is depicted in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406915-fig-0007">7d,e</a>. The charge separation in CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub> heterostructure clearly indicates a significant internal electric field, providing a robust impetus for the migration of electrons and ions. As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406915-fig-0007">7f</a>, the transfer of some electrons from Na to MoSe<sub>2</sub> and CoSe is clearly demonstrated, indicating that the heterojunction establishes a complete and stable charge diffusion path, which further enhances reaction kinetics and structure stability. The ionic diffusion paths in MoSe<sub>2</sub>, CoSe and CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>, along with the calculated migration energy barriers of Na<sup>+</sup>, are presented in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406915-fig-0007">7g–i</a>, the diffusion energy barrier of the CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub> heterostructure at 1.07&nbsp;eV is notably lower compared to the CoSe (1.49&nbsp;eV) and MoSe<sub>2</sub> (1.35&nbsp;eV), suggesting the fast and easy diffusion process of Na<sup>+</sup> in the CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub> heterostructure.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202406915-fig-0007"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/7d749add-e595-4468-8c93-2a9fbcd3b1e3/adfm202406915-fig-0007-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/7d749add-e595-4468-8c93-2a9fbcd3b1e3/adfm202406915-fig-0007-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/34b325ba-159c-408b-81d9-9c69fc36dbe0/adfm202406915-fig-0007-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/7d749add-e595-4468-8c93-2a9fbcd3b1e3/adfm202406915-fig-0007-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 7<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202406915-fig-0007&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202406915" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) DOS curves of MoSe<sub>2</sub>, CoSe, and CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>. b) Schematic representation of Na+ adsorption sites on CoSe, MoSe<sub>2</sub>, and CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub> and c) Na<sup>+</sup> adsorption energy of the proposed configurations. Charge density differences within CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub> heterojunction: d) side view and e) top view, and f) charge density difference of Na<sup>+</sup> adsorbed by CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub> heterostructure (The yellow and blue regions correspond to charge depletion and aggregation, respectively). Diffusion paths and corresponding energy barriers of g) CoSe, h) MoSe<sub>2</sub>, and i) CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>To further investigate the potential applications of the CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C anode, the coin-type full cells composed of Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>@rGO (NVP@rGO) cathode and CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C anode were assembled. Furthermore, the XRD pattern of NVP@rGO is depicted in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S24</a> (Supporting Information). <b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406915-fig-0008">8a</a> shows the schematically illustration. The NVP@rGO and CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C half-cells exhibit initial charge/discharge capacities of 90.1/88.5&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> and 394.4/532.0&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.2&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, respectively (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406915-fig-0008">8b</a>). Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406915-fig-0008">8c</a> displays the GCD curves for the NVP@rGO//CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C full cell at 0.2&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, indicating that the working voltage platform is consistent with the voltage platform difference between the cathode and anode, and the initial charge/discharge capacities are 494.3/329.0&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, corresponding to a high CE of 66.6%. The cycling performances of the coin-type full cells at 0.5&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> are displayed in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406915-fig-0008">8d</a>, and the specific capacities could be remained at 234.6/230.5&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 340 cycles. Meanwhile, the coin-type full cells deliver high capacity and satisfactory cycling performance at 0.1 and 0.2&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> (Figures&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S25</a> and&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S26</a>, Supporting Information). The rate performance of the full cell has been further tested (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406915-fig-0008">8e</a>), in which the average discharge specific capacities are 307.3, 277.3, 265.1, and 243.5&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.05, 0.1, 0.4, and 0.8&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, respectively. Upon returning the current density to 0.05&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, the specific capacities were rejuvenated to 270/268.7&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. The full cells could achieve an energy density of 123.07&nbsp;Wh&nbsp;kg<sup>−1</sup> at the power density of 27.83&nbsp;W&nbsp;kg<sup>−1</sup> and maintains an energy density of 99.07&nbsp;Wh&nbsp;kg<sup>−1</sup> even at a relatively comparatively elevated power density of 198.14&nbsp;W&nbsp;kg<sup>−1</sup> (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S27</a>, Supporting Information). Furthermore, the pouch-type full-cells were also triumphantly fabricated and demonstrated the light bulb, and the light bulb can still be lit up safely and efficiently after bending into different angles (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406915-fig-0008">8f–i</a>, Supporting Information). The above electrochemical performances indicate the NVP@rGO//CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C full cells have promising application potential.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202406915-fig-0008"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/2094a9d5-c7e0-49f7-9fd6-f240fadf54ae/adfm202406915-fig-0008-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/2094a9d5-c7e0-49f7-9fd6-f240fadf54ae/adfm202406915-fig-0008-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/95ff373c-71b1-43be-b417-26c16a444607/adfm202406915-fig-0008-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/2094a9d5-c7e0-49f7-9fd6-f240fadf54ae/adfm202406915-fig-0008-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 8<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202406915-fig-0008&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202406915" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) Schematic illustration of the NVP@rGO//CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C full-cell, b) GCD curves of NVP@rGO and CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C in half-cell. c) GCD curves at 0.2&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, d) cycling performance at 0.5&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>and e) rate performance of the coin-type full cells. f–i) pouch-type full cells powered LED lights.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
      </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adfm202406915-sec-0030">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adfm202406915-sec-0030-title">3 Conclusion</h2>
         
         <p>In summary, the CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C nanosphere heterostructure composites were successfully constructed by solvothermal and subsequent selenization and carbonization processes. The experimental studies coupled with theoretical calculations indicate that the heterointerface engineering between CoSe and MoSe<sub>2</sub> could accelerate the kinetics of Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion and charge transfer, taking advantage of the effect from the build-in electric field. Likewise, glycerol-derived carbon aids in improving electrical conductivity and structural integrity. Based on these advantages, the CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C anode exhibits a high capacity of 428.1&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.2&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> and excellent ultra-stable cycling lifespan over 10000 cycles with only 0.01781&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> decay per cycle at 2.0&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> for SIBs. Furthermore, the NVP@rGO//CoSe/MoSe<sub>2</sub>-C full cells were packaged and delivers satisfactory electrochemical performance. Remarkably, the pouch-type full cells were also triumphantly fabricated and preliminary evidenced their feasibility and safety performance. Moreover, in situ XRD, ex situ XPS and HRTEM analyses reveal the Na<sup>+</sup> storage mechanism, which is founded on the conversion reaction of CoSe and MoSe<sub>2</sub>. This work provides a prospective approach to utilize engineering heterostructure and introducing homogeneous carbon to design highly efficient anodes for SIBs.</p>
         </section>
      <div class="article-section__content">
